## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A(t), which is the central object in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, the most likely models are kinetic rate laws expressed as ODEs dA_dt = r(A,t) such as zero/first/second order, reversible relaxation to equilibrium, autocatalysis, or time-dependent rate coefficients.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production; linear A vs t)
- First-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; exponential A(t))
- Second-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction; 1/A linear in t)
- General n-th order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order fitting)
- Reversible first-order relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to steady state Aâ†’c1)
- Logistic/autocatalytic with carrying capacity: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth then saturation; e.g., autocatalysis with depletion)
- Autocatalysis with baseline term: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (runaway growth/accelerated production regimes)
- Rational (inhibition/limited-rate) form: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective rate saturates at high A due to inhibition/transport limits)
- Rational (activation) form: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 / (A + c1) (second-order at low A, first-order-like at high A)
- Time-dependent first-order coefficient (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (changing conditions/catalyst activity over time)
- Time-dependent first-order coefficient (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (slowly varying rate constant; aging/heating protocols)
- Periodic forcing of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (externally modulated environment/illumination cycles)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear A vs t suggests zero-order: dA_dt approximately constant (mass-transfer-limited or saturated catalyst).
- Exponential A(t) (straight line in ln(A) vs t) suggests first-order: dA_dt proportional to A.
- Linear 1/A vs t suggests second-order: dA_dt proportional to A**2.
- Presence of a nonzero steady state Aâ†’A_eq implies a relaxation form like dA_dt proportional to (A - A_eq).
- Sigmoid A(t) with inflection (initial acceleration then slowing) indicates autocatalytic/logistic structure dA_dt proportional to A*(c - A).
- Rates that plateau with increasing A indicate rational forms such as A/(A+c) (effective saturation or inhibition/transport limitation).
- Changing apparent rate constant over time (different slopes in ln(A) vs t across windows) suggests k(t) models like exp(c*t) or (c0+c1*t).
- Oscillatory variations in dA_dt at fixed A suggest explicit time forcing via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t).
- If dA_dt changes sign near some A value, include additive offset or equilibrium term (A - c) to allow production vs consumption regimes.
